Normatively Used Namespaces:

This specification doesn't declare its own namespaces. However, it provides [JSON] specific methods to represent objects and properties from the following namespaces:

Namespaces used normatively in both JLIFF Version 1.0 serializations (shared between [XLIFF 2.1] and [XLIFF 2.0]:

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:document:2.0

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:matches:2.0

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:glossary:2.0

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:fs:2.0

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:metadata:2.0

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:resourcedata:2.0

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:sizerestriction:2.0

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:validation:2.0

Namespaces used normatively only in the JLIFF serialization 2.1 (from [XLIFF 2.1]):

  • https://www.w3.org/2005/11/its/

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:itsm:2.1

Namespaces used normatively only in the JLIFF serialization 2.0 (from [XLIFF 2.0]):

  • urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:changetracking:2.0

Abstract:

This document defines version 1.0 of JLIFF, the JSON Localization Interchange Fragment Format, based on the XLIFF 2 Object Model that has been in turn based on the XLIFF 2 Family of Standards. The purpose of JLIFF is to provide standard JSON serialization methods for all XLIFF OM objects, their relationships, and data models, so that Localization tools can exchange translation and localization task data in an interoperable way.

Same as [JSON] (its parent etiquette), JLIFF concentrates on real time exchange scenarios. Thanks to the fact that JLIFF and XLIFF (the original XML serialization) share the same Object Model [LIOM], implementers of both formats can rely on and benefit from the semantic and behavioral match between those two interchange formats.

Since JLIFF primarily targets real time API exchanges, it is capable of expressing different levels of fragments corresponding to various structural parts of the XLIFF OM and possibly related XLIFF Documents.

1 Introduction

JSON Localization Interchange Fragment Format (JLIFF), a serialization of the LIOM (Localization Interchange Object Model), which is the XLIFF 2 Object Model, has been designed by a group of multilingual content publishers, software providers, localization service providers, localization tools providers, and researchers. It is intended to give any multilingual content owner a reliable and interoperable JSON serialization of the said object and data model. XLIFF 2 has been providing a reliable XML based interchange file format understood by any localization provider, using any conformant localization tool. The primary focus of this JSON serialization specification of the shared Object Model is to ensure lossless Interchange between JSON and XML pipelines, or indeed other pipelines serialized in other ways, as long as they are based on the same underlying Object Model. While the primary focus is on lossless Interchange, toolmakers, service providers, and content owners are encouraged to stick to the shared Object Model [LIOM] also while designing their internal processing and messaging formats, as this will make the mapping to the standardized Interchange format serializations of this Object Model, such as JLIFF or XLIFF, so much easier.

All text is normative unless otherwise labeled. The following common methods are used for labeling portions of this specification as informative and hence non-normative:

Appendices and sections marked as "(Informative)" or "Non-Normative" in title,
Notes (sections with the "Note" title),
Warnings (sections with the "Warning" title),
Examples (mainly example code listings, tree diagrams, but also any inline examples or illustrative exemplary lists in otherwise normative text),
Schema and other validation artifacts listings (the corresponding artifacts are normative, not their listings).

1.1 Terminology

1.1.1 Key words

The key words MUST, MUST NOT, REQUIRED, SHALL, SHALL NOT, SHOULD, SHOULD NOT, RECOMMENDED, MAY, and OPTIONAL are to be interpreted as described in [RFC 2119].

1.1.2 Definitions

Agent

any application or tool that generates (creates), reads, edits, writes, processes, stores, renders or otherwise handles JLIFF Instances.

Agent is the most general application conformance target that subsumes all other specialized user agents disregarding whether they are defined in this specification or not.

Enrich, Enriching

the process of associating metadata and resources with the Extracted JLIFF payload

Processing Requirements

  • Enriching MAY happen at the time of Extraction.

Note

Extractor knowledge of the native format is not assumed while Enriching.

Enricher, Enricher Agent

any Agent that performs the Enriching process

Extract, Extraction

the process of encoding localizable content from a native content or User Interface format as JLIFF Instances, so that localizable parts of the content in the source language are available for Translation into the target language along with the necessary context information

Extractor, Extractor Agent

any Agent that performs the Extraction process

Merge, Merging

the process of importing JLIFF payload back to the originating native format, based on the full knowledge of the Extraction mechanism, so that the localized content or User Interface strings replace the source language in the native format

Merger, Merger Agent

an Agent that performs the Merge process

Warning

Unless specified otherwise, any Merger is deemed to have the same knowledge of the native format as the Extractor throughout the specification.

Mergers independent of Extractors can succeed, but it is out of scope of this specification to specify interoperability for Merging back without the full Extractor knowledge of the native format.

Modify, Modification

the process of changing core and module based structural and inline objects that were previously created by other Writers

Processing Requirements

  • JLIFF objects MAY be Modified and Enriched at the same time.

Note

Extractor or Enricher knowledge of the native format is not assumed while Modifying.

Modifier, Modifier Agent

an Agent that performs the Modification process

Translation, Translate

a rendering of the meaning of the source text, expressed in the target language

Writer, Writer Agent

an Agent that creates, generates, or otherwise writes JLIFF Instances for whatever purpose, including but not limited to Extractor, Modifier, and Enricher Agents.

Note

Since JLIFF is intended as an exchange format rather than a processing format, many applications will need to generate JLIFF Instances from their internal processing formats, even in cases when they are processing JLIFF Instances created by another Extractor.

1.1.3 Key concepts

JLIFF Core

The core of JLIFF Version 1.0 consists of the minimum set of JSON objects, properties, and values required to (a) prepare a JLIFF Instance that contains text Extracted from one or more files for localization, (b) allow it to be completed with the Translation of the Extracted text, and (c) allow the generation of Translated versions of the original document.

The namespace that corresponds to the core subset of JLIFF Version 1.0 is "urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:document:2.0".

Note

Vanilla JSON is not capable of expressing namespaces. Nevertheless, JLIFF adopts two prefix conventions that allow for representing LIOM and XLIFF namespaces to be able to make use of LIOM modularity.

JLIFF Core object or property names are not prefixed either in JLIFF Instances or in the JLIFF JSON Schema.

Note

JLIFF Version 1.0 contains prose and JSON schema specifications of JLIFF 2.0 and JLIFF 2.1. These two serializations share JLIFF Core 2.0 that maps one-to-one to XLIFF Core 2.0 that is shared between XLIFF Version 2.1 and XLIFF Version 2.0

Two different schema instances are provided, JLIFF 2.1 and JLIFF 2.0. The prose specifications contains conditional provisions for JLIFF serialization 2.1 and JLIFF serialization 2.0 in this document.

JLIFF Module

A module is an OPTIONAL set of JSON objects and properties that stores information about a process applied to a JLIFF Instance and the data incorporated into the instance as result of that process.

Note

Each official module defined for JLIFF Vesrion 1.0 has its grammar defined in a JSON Schema integrated with the core JSON schema. Two different schema instances are provided, JLIFF serialization 2.1 and JLIFF serialization 2.0.

JLIFF-defined (objects and properties)

All JLIFF-defined objects and properties are specified in this document. The extent of JLIFF-defined is different for the JLIFF serialization 2.1 and JLIFF serialization 2.0. This corresponds to the lists of namespaces used normatively in either of the serializations stated in this specification.

JLIFF Instance

JLIFF Instance is a conforming JSON text according to [ECMA-JSON] Clause 2 that validates against the schema for JLIFF serialization 2.1 or JLIFF serialization 2.0.

2 Conformance

  1. Document Conformance

    1. JLIFF is a JSON application, therefore conformant JLIFF Instances MUST be well formed and valid JSON files according to [ECMA-JSON] Clause 2.

    2. Conformant JLIFF Instances MUST be valid instances of one of the official Core JLIFF Schemas that are parts of this multipart Work Product,

      http://docs.oasis-open.org/xliff-omos/jliff/v1.0/wd01/schemas/jliff-schema-2.1.json, for the JLIFF serialization 2.1.

      http://docs.oasis-open.org/xliff-omos/jliff/v1.0/wd01/schemas/jliff-schema-2.0.json, for the JLIFF serialization 2.0.

    3. As not all aspects of the JLIFF specification can be expressed in terms of JSON Schemas, conformant JLIFF Instances MUST also comply with all relevant objects and properties definitions, normative usage descriptions, and Constraints specified in this specification document.

    4. JLIFF Instances MAY contain custom extensions, as defined in the Extension Mechanisms section.

  2. Application Conformance

    1. JLIFF Writers MUST create conformant JLIFF Instances to be considered JLIFF compliant.

    2. Agents processing conformant JLIFF Instances that contain custom extensions are not REQUIRED to understand and process non-JLIFF objects or properties. However, conformant applications SHOULD preserve existing custom extensions when processing conformant JLIFF Instances, provided that the objects or properties that contain custom extensions are not removed according to JLIIFF Processing Requirements or the extension's own processing requirements.

    3. All Agents MUST comply with Processing Requirements for otherwise unspecified Agents or without a specifically set target Agent.

    4. Specialized Agents defined in this specification - this is Extractor, Merger, Writer, Modifier, and Enricher Agents - MUST comply with the Processing Requirements targeting their specifically defined type of Agent on top of Processing Requirements targeting all Agents as per point c. above.

    5. JLIFF is a format explicitly designed for exchanging data among various Agents. Thus, a conformant JLIFF application MUST be able to accept JLIFF Instances it had written after those JLIFF Instances were Modified or Enriched by a different application, provided that:

      1. The processed files are conformant JLIFF Instances,

      2. in a state compliant with all relevant Processing Requirements.

  3. Backwards Compatibility

    1. Conformant applications are REQUIRED to support both serializations defined in this specifcation.

    2. No previous versions of JLIFF exist.

Note

JLIFF Instances conformant to this specification are suitable for exchange of data with XLIFF 2 Documents based processes. Normative Appendix C [insert coss reference once created] provides requirements for and guidance on roundtripping XLIFF 2 data using JLIFF, i.e. how to import XLIFF 2 data to JLIFF and how to export JLIFF data to XLIFF 2.0 or XLIFF 2.1.

3 Fragment Identification

This specification defines how Agents MUST interpret the fragment identifiers in IRIs pointing to JLIFF Instances.

Note

Since JLIFF uses the same fragid mechanism as XLIFF. XLIFF and JLIFF identifiers will work interchangeably across the JLIFF and XLIFF media types.

Note

Note that some identifiers can change during the localization process. For example on resegmentation or when regrouping or not data objects depending on how tools treat identical original data.

Constraints

  • A fragment identifier MUST match the following format:

    <expression>      ::= "#" ["/"] <selector>
                      {<selectorSeparator> <selector>}
<selector>        ::= [<prefix> <prefixSeparator>] <id>
<prefix>          ::= NMTOKEN
<id>              ::= NMTOKEN
<prefixSeparator> ::= "="
<selectorSeparator>  ::= "/"

  • There MUST NOT be two identical prefixes in the expression.

  • When used, the following selectors MUST be declared in this order: file selector, group selector and unit selector.

  • The selectors for modules or extensions, <note>, <segment> or <ignorable> or source inline elements, target inline elements and <data> have the following constraints:

    • Only one of them MAY be used in the expression.

    • The one used MUST be the last selector of the expression.

Warning

Please note that due to the above Constraints, referencing fragments using third party namespaces within Modules or extensions (including but not limited to XLIFF Core or the Metadata Module) is not possible. This is to restrict the complexity of the fragment identification mechanism, as it would otherwise have potentially unlimited depth.

3.1 Selectors for Core Objects

  • The prefix f indicates an anonymous file object id and the value of that id is unique among all anonymous file object REQUIRED id property values within the enclosing anonymous jliff object.

  • The prefix g indicates an anonymous subitem object "kind" : "group" id and the value of that id is unique among all anonymous subitem object "kind" : "group" id attribute values within the enclosing anonymous file object or anonymous jliff object.

  • The prefix u indicates an anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit" id and the value of that id is unique among all anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit" id property values within the enclosing anonymous file object or anonymous jliff object.

  • The prefix n indicates a anonymous note object id and the value of that id is unique among all anonymous note object id property values within the same anonymous notes array.

  • The prefix d indicates a <data> id and the value of that id is unique among all <data> id attribute values within the enclosing <unit> element. [pending modification of descriptions for data and original data objects/arrays]

  • The prefix t indicates an id for an inline object contained in an anonymous target property array and the value of that id is unique within the enclosing anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit" with the exception of the matching inline objects contained in its sibling anonymous source property array.

  • No prefix indicates an id for an anonymous subunit item "kind" : "segment" or an anonymous subunit object "kind" : "ignorable" or an inline element in the anonymous source property array and the value of that id is unique within the enclosing anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit" with the exception of the matching inline objects contained its sibling anonymous target property array.

3.2 Selectors for Modules and Extensions

A selector for a module or an extension uses a registered prefix and the value of that id is unique within the immediate enclosing anonymous file object, anonymous subitem object "kind" : "group", or anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit".

Constraints

  • The prefix of a module or an extension MUST be an NMTOKEN longer than 1 character and MUST be defined in the module or extension specification.

  • The prefix of a module or an extension MUST be registered with the XLIFF TC.

  • A given module or extension namespace URI MUST be associated with a single prefix.

  • A prefix MAY be associated with more than one namespace URI (to allow for example different versions of a given module or extension to use the same prefix).

See also the constraints related to how IDs need to be specified in extensions (which applies for modules as well).

3.3 Relative References

Fragment identifiers that do not start with a character / (U+002F) are relative to their location in the document, or to the document being processed.

Any unit, group or file selector missing to resolve the relative reference is obtained from the immediate enclosing unit, group or file object.

3.4 Examples

Given the following JLIFF Instance:

{ "jliff": "2.1",
  "srcLang": "en-US",
  "trgLang": "fr-FR",
  "files": [
    { "id": "f1",
      "kind": "file",
      "notes": [
        { "id": "n1",
          "text": "note for file." }
      ],
      "subfiles": [
        { "canResegment": "no",
          "id": "u1",
          "kind": "unit",
          "notes": [
            { "id": "n1",
              "text": "note for unit" }
          ],
          "subunits": [
            { "id": "s1",
              "kind": "segment",
              "source": [
                { "id": "1",
                  "kind": "sc" },
                { "text": "Hello " },
                { "id": "m1",
                  "kind": "sm",
                  "type": "term" },
                { "text": "World" },
                { "kind": "em",
                   "startRef": "m1" },
                { "text": "!" },
                { "kind": "ec",
                  "startRef": "1" }
              ],
              "target": [
                { "id": "1",
                  "kind": "sc" },
                { "text": "Bonjour le " },
                { "id": "m1",
                  "kind": "sm",
                  "type": "term" },
                { "text": "Monde" },
                { "kind": "em",
                  "startRef": "m1" },
                { "text": "!" },
                { "kind": "ec",
                  "startRef": "1" }
              ] }
          ] }
      ] }
  ]
}

You can have the following fragment identifiers:

  • #f=f1/u=u1/1 refers to the element <pc id="1"> of the source content of the element <unit id="u1">.

  • #f=f1/u=u1/t=1 refers to the element <pc id="1"> of the target content of the element <unit id="u1">.

  • #f=f1/n=n1 refers to the element <note id="n1"> of the element <file id="f1">.

  • #f=f1/u=u1/n=n1 refers to the element <note id="n1"> of the element <unit id="u1">.

  • #f=f1/u=u1/s1 refers to the element <segment id="s1"> of the element <unit id="u1">.

  • Assuming the extension defined by the namespace URI myNamespaceURI has registered the prefix myprefix, the expression #f=f1/u=u1/myprefix=x1 refers to the element <my:element id="x1"> of the element <unit id="u1">.

4 The Core Specification

JLIFF is a bilingual JSON interchange format designed to contain text that needs Translation, its corresponding translations, and auxiliary data that makes the Translation process possible.

At creation time, a JLIFF Instance MAY contain only text in the source language. Translations expressed in the target language MAY be added at a later time.

JLIFF postulates several possible root objects. The highest level object corresponds to LIF.

The LIFF object corresponds to the root element of an XLIFF Document, which is <xliff>.

WORK IN PROGRESS!!! THE FOLLOWING PARTS OF THE SPECIFICATION NEED RESTATED IN AN XML INDEPENDENT WAY It contains a collection of <file> elements. Typically, each <file> element contains a set of <unit> elements that contain the text to be translated in the <source> child of one or more <segment> elements. Translations are stored in the <target> child of each <segment> element.

4.1 General Processing Requirements

  • An Agent processing a valid XLIFF Document that contains XLIFF-defined elements and attributes that it cannot handle MUST preserve those elements and attributes.

  • An Agent processing a valid XLIFF Document that contains custom elements and attributes that it cannot handle SHOULD preserve those elements and attributes.

4.2 Elements

This section contains a description of all elements used in XLIFF Core.

4.2.1 Tree Structure

Legend:

1 = one
+ = one or more
? = zero or one
* = zero or more
jliff
|
+---<file> +
  |
  +---<skeleton> ?
  | |
  | +---<other> *
  |
  +---<other> *
  |
  +---<notes> ?
  | |
  | +---<note> +
  |
  +---At least one of (<unit> OR <group>)
      | |
      | +---<unit>
      |   |
      |   +---<other> *
      |   |
      |   +---<notes> ?
      |   | |
      |   | +---<note> +
      |   |
      |   +---<originalData> ?
      |   | |
      |   | +---<data> +
      |   |
      |   +---At least one of (<segment> OR <ignorable>)
      |       | |
      |       | +---<segment>
      |       |   |
      |       |   +---<source> 1
      |       |   |
      |       |   +---<target> ?
      |       |
      |       +---<ignorable>
      |           |
      |           +---<source> 1
      |           |
      |           +---<target> ?
      |
      +---<group>
          |
          +---<other> *
          |
          +---<notes> ?
          | |
          | +---<note> +
          |
          +---At least one of (<unit> OR <group>)

4.2.2 Structural Elements

The structural elements used in XLIFF Core are: jliff, file, subitem, skeleton, group, unit, subunit, segment, ignorable, notes, note, originalData, originalDataDir, data, source and target.

4.2.2.1 anonymous jliff object with property "files|subfiles|subgroups|subunits"

Root object for JLIFF documents.

Type: object.

- One or more <file> elements

Properties:

- version, REQUIRED
- srcLang, REQUIRED
- trgLang, OPTIONAL
- xml:space, OPTIONAL
- attributes from other namespaces, OPTIONAL

Constraints

  • The "trgLang" property is REQUIRED if and only if the JLIFF Document contains "target" array property in segment or ignorable.

4.2.2.2 anonymous file object

Container for localization material extracted from an entire single document, or another high level self contained logical node in a content structure that cannot be described in the terms of documents.

Note

Sub-document artifacts such as particular sheets, pages, chapters and similar are better mapped onto the group object. The file object is intended for the highest logical level. For instance a collection of papers would map to a single JLIFF Document, each paper will be represented with one file object, whereas chapters and subsections will map onto file property "subfiles" with an array of group objects.

Type: object.

Properties:

- "skeleton", a skeleton object, OPTIONAL
- "notes", a non-empty array of note objects, optional
- "subfiles", a non-empty array of unit and group objects, required
- "id", an id string, REQUIRED
- "canResegment", a canResegment string, OPTIONAL
- "original", an original string, OPTIONAL
- "translate", a translate string, OPTIONAL
- "srcDir", a srcDir string, OPTIONAL
- "trgDir", a trgDir string, OPTIONAL
- [NEED A SECTION TO DESCRIBE xml:space ROUNDTRIPPING]xml:space, OPTIONAL
- other none-core properties, OPTIONAL,

Constraints

  • The following OPTIONAL JLIFF Module properties are explicitly allowed by the wildcard other provided that they don't violate its own module's Constraints or Processing Requirements:

    • Properties allowed in both JLIFF 2.1 and JLIFF 2.0:

      - "fs_fs", a fs_fs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
      - "fs_subFs", a fs_subFs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
      - "mda_metadata", a mda_metadata object.
      - "res_resourceData", a res_resourceData object.
      - "slr_profiles", a slr_profiles object.
      - "slr_data", a slr_data object.
      - "slr_storageRestriction", a slr_storageRestriction string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
      - "slr_sizeRestriction", a slr_sizeRestriction string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
      - "slr_sizeInfo", a slr_sizeInfo string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
      - "slr_sizeInfoRef", a slr_sizeInfoRef string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
      - "val_validation", a val_validation object.

    • Properties allowed only in JLIFF 2.1

      - "its_locQualityRatingProfileRef", a its_locQualityRatingProfileRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_locQualityRatingScore", a its_locQualityRatingScore number between 0 and 100 inclusive.
      - "its_locQualityRatingScoreThreshold", a its_locQualityRatingScoreThreshold number between 0 and 100 inclusive.
      - "its_locQualityRatingVote", a its_locQualityRatingVote integer.
      - "its_locQualityRatingVoteThreshold", a its_locQualityRatingVoteThreshold integer.
      - "its_annotatorsRef", a its_annotatorsRef object.
      - "its_org", a its_org string.
      - "its_orgRef", a its_orgRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_person", a its_person string.
      - "its_personRef", a its_personRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_provenanceRecordsRef", a its_provenanceRecordsRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_revOrg", a its_revOrg string.
      - "its_revOrgRef", a its_revOrgRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_revPerson", a its_revPerson string.
      - "its_revPersonRef", a its_revPersonRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_revTool", a its_revTool string.
      - "its_revToolRef", a its_revToolRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_tool", a its_tool string.
      - "its_toolRef", a its_toolRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_provenanceRecords", a non-empty array of its_provenanceRecords objects.
      - "its_taClassRef", a its_taClassRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_taConfidence", a its_taConfidence number between 0 and 1 inclusive.
      - "its_taSource", a its_taSource string.
      - "its_taIdent", a its_taIdent string.
      - "its_taIdentRef", a its_taIdentRef string with IRI value.
      - "itsm_domains", a itsm_domains a non-empty array of non-empty strings not containing the , chatacter (U+002C).

    • Properties allowed only in JLIFF 2.0

      - "ctr_changeTrack", a ctr_changeTrack object.

  • The following optional JLIFF Extension property is allowed:

    - "userdata", a userdata object.

  • No other properties are permitted.

4.2.2.3 anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit|group"

This type is a union of two subtypes governed by the value of the key kind.

This object is an anonymous container for a dynamic structure of unit and group objects. Unit objects hold the extracted translatable source text, aligned with the Translated text. Group objects provide a way to organize units into a structured hierarchy.

Type: object with property "kind" : "unit" or "kind" : "group"

- elements from other namespaces, OPTIONAL
- Zero or one <notes> elements followed by
- Zero or one <originalData> element followed by
- One or more <segment> or <ignorable> elements in any order.

Properties:

- id, REQUIRED
- name, OPTIONAL
- canResegment, OPTIONAL
- translate, OPTIONAL
- srcDir, OPTIONAL
- trgDir, OPTIONAL
- xml:space, OPTIONAL
- type, OPTIONAL
- attributes from other namespaces, OPTIONAL
4.2.2.4 skeleton

Container for non-translatable material pertaining to the parent file object.

Type: object.

Either

- Non-translatable text
- elements from other namespaces

or

- is empty.

Properties:

- "href", an href object, REQUIRED

Constraints

  • The property "href" is REQUIRED if and only if the skeleton element is empty.

Processing Requirements

  • Modifiers and Enrichers processing an JLIFF Document that contains a skeleton object MUST NOT change that object or its property, or its content.

  • Extractors creating an JLIFF Document with a skeleton object MUST leave the skeleton object empty if and only if they specify the attribute href.

4.2.2.5 anonymous subitem object "kind" : "group"

Provides a way to organize units into a structured hierarchy.

Note that this is especially useful for mirroring a source format's hierarchical structure.

Type: object.

Properties:

- "id", a id string with NMTOKEN value, REQUIRED
- "kind", a kind string, REQUIRED with fixed value "group"
- "name", a name string, OPTIONAL
- "canResegment", a canResegment string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL with default value "yes"
- "translate", a translate object, OPTIONAL
- "srcDir", a srcDir object, OPTIONAL
- "trgDir", a trgDir object, OPTIONAL
- "type", a type object, OPTIONAL
- "notes", an array of note objects, OPTIONAL
- "subgroups", an array of subitem objects, OPTIONAL
- [NEED A SECTION TO DESCRIBE xml:space ROUNDTRIPPING]xml:space, OPTIONAL

4.2.2.6 anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit"

4.2.2.7 anonymous subunit object "kind" : "segment|ignorable"

This type is a union of two subtypes governed by the value of the key kind.

This object is an anonymous container to hold in its aligned pair of children objects the minimum portion of translatable source text and its Translation in the given Segmentation.

Type: object with property "kind" : "segment" or "kind" : "ignorable"

- kind, REQUIRED
- id, OPTIONAL
- One source object
- Zero or one <target> element

Properties:

- canResegment, OPTIONAL
- state, OPTIONAL
- subState, OPTIONAL
4.2.2.8 anonymous subunit object "kind" : "segment"

This object is a container to hold in its aligned pair of children objects the minimum portion of translatable source text and its Translation in the given Segmentation.

Properties:

- "id", a id string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "kind", a kind string, REQUIRED with fixed value "segment"
- "canResegment", a canResegment string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL with default value "yes"
- "state", a state string of value "initial", "translated", "reviewed", or "final", OPTIONAL with default value "initial"
- "subState", a subState string, OPTIONAL
- "sourceXmlLang", a "sourceXmlLang" string, OPTIONAL with a [BCP 47] tag value
- "targetXmlLang", a "targetXmlLang" string, OPTIONAL with a [BCP 47] tag value
- "targetOrder", a "targetOrder" number, OPTIONAL with a positive integer value
- "source", a non-empty array of inline objects, REQUIRED
- "target", a non-empty array of inline objects, OPTIONAL
4.2.2.9 anonymous subunit object "kind" : "ignorable"

Part of the extracted content that is not included in a segment (and therefore not translatable). For example tools can use <ignorable> to store the white space and/or codes that are between two segments.

Type: object.

Properties:

- "id", a id string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "kind", a kind string, REQUIRED with fixed value "ignorable"
- "sourceXmlLang", a "sourceXmlLang" string, OPTIONAL with a [BCP 47] tag value
- "targetXmlLang", a "targetXmlLang" string, OPTIONAL with a [BCP 47] tag value
- "targetOrder", a "targetOrder" number, OPTIONAL with a positive integer value
- "source", a non-empty array of inline objects, REQUIRED
- "target", a non-empty array of inline objects, OPTIONAL
4.2.2.10 anonymous array of note objects

Collection of comments pertaining to the given node including all of its descendants

Type:

- One or more note objects
4.2.2.11 anonymous note object with a required "text" property

This is a JLIFF specific object to present end-user readable comments and annotations. A note can contain information about source, target, unit, group, or file objects.

Type: object.

Properties:

- "text", a text string, REQUIRED
- "id", a id string, OPTIONAL
- "appliesTo", an appliesTo string, OPTIONAL
- "category", a category string, OPTIONAL
- "priority", a priority string, OPTIONAL

Constraints

  • The following optional JLIFF Module properties are explicitly allowed by the wildcard other:

    - "fs_fs", a fs_fs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - "fs_subFs", a fs_subFs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.

  • The following optional JLIFF Extension property is allowed:

    - "userdata", a userdata object.

  • No other properties are permitted.

4.2.2.12 originalData object

Unit-level collection of original data for the inline codes.

Type: object.

Properties:

- properties represent a dictionary of NMTOKEN and string value pairs , REQUIRED

Contraints

  • The NMTOKEN key MUST be unique within the collection to make the original data strings addressable from "dataref" properties within inline objects of the same unit.

4.2.2.13 originalDataDir object

Unit-level collection of original data directionality for the inline codes.

Type: object.

Properties:

- properties represent a dictionary of NMTOKEN and "dir" value pairs , REQUIRED

Contraints

  • The NMTOKEN key MUST be unique within the collection to make the original data strings addressable from "dataRef" properties within inline objects of the same unit.

  • Each NMTOKEN key in the collection MUST correspond to an NMTOKEN key in the "originalData" dictionary object in the same unit.

4.2.2.14 data <not used in JLIFF described in originalData>

Storage for the original data of an inline code.

Type:

- Non-translatable text
- Zero, one or more <cp> elements.

Non-translatable text and <cp> elements MAY appear in any order.

Attributes:

- id, REQUIRED
- dir, OPTIONAL
- xml:space, OPTIONAL, the value is restricted to preserve on this element
4.2.2.15 "source" property

Portion of text to be translated.

Contains a non-empty anonymous array of inline objects:

- Zero, one or more text objects
- Zero, one or more ph objects
- Zero, one or more sc objects
- Zero, one or more ec objects
- Zero, one or more sm objects
- Zero, one or more em objects

The text, code, and marker objects appear in a significant order.

4.2.2.16 "target" property

Property to keep the translation of the sibling source property.

Contains a non-empty anonymous array of inline objects:

- Zero, one or more text objects
- Zero, one or more ph objects
- Zero, one or more sc objects
- Zero, one or more ec objects
- Zero, one or more sm objects
- Zero, one or more em objects

The text, code, and marker objects appear in a significant order.

4.2.3 Inline Elements

The XLIFF Core inline elements at the <source> or <target> level are: <cp>, <ph>, <pc>, <sc>, <ec>, <mrk>, <sm> and <em>.

The elements at the <unit> level directly related to inline elements are: <originalData> and <data>.

4.2.3.1 Roundtripping XLIFF <cp/>

XLIFF <cp> represents a Unicode character that is invalid in XML.

Type:

JLIFF doesn't have an equivalent to XLIFF <cp>

Example in XLIFF:

<unit id="1">
  <segment>
    <source>Ctrl+C=<cp hex="0003"/></source>
  </segment>
</unit>

Equivalent of the above example in JLIFF:

WIP 

^C [Oxyegn doesn't accept the literal even in CDATA]
\u
"Ctrl+C=\u0003"

The example above shows a character U+0003 (Control C) as it has to be represented in XLIFF. As the character ETX is legal in JSON, the <cp hex="0003"> becomes the literal of "^C" or "ETX" in the JLIFF serialization. in case of mixed XLIFF and JLIFF pipelines the conversion mechanism needs to be able to "cp-encode" XML illegal characters in LIFF on the fly or vice versa to replace the "cp-encoded" XLIFF representations with their literal equivalents in JLIFF.

Processing Requirements

  • JLIFF Writers receiving XLIFF <cp> MUST replace the code with the corresponding literal character given by the XLIFF https://docs.oasis-open.org/xliff/xliff-core/v2.1/os/xliff-core-v2.1-os.html#hexhex attribute.

  • XLIFF Writers receiving illegal XML characters (Unicode characters with hexadecimal codes from 0000 to 10FFFF) MUST replace each XML illegal character with the XLIFF <cp> element using the corresponding https://docs.oasis-open.org/xliff/xliff-core/v2.1/os/xliff-core-v2.1-os.html#hexhex attribute.

  • XLIFF Writers MUST NOT encode valid XML characters of the content using <cp>.

4.2.3.2 ph

Represents a standalone code of the original format.

Type: object.

This element is always empty.

Used in:

source array or target array

Properties:

- "kind", a kind string with fixed value "ph", REQUIRED
- "canCopy". a canCopy string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canDelete", acanDelete string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canOverlap", a canOverlap string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canReorder", a canReorder string with value "yes", "no", or "firstNo", OPTIONAL with default value "yes"
- "copyOf", a copyOf string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "dataRef", a dataRef string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "disp", a disp string, OPTIONAL
- "equiv", a equiv string, OPTIONAL
- "id", a id string with NMTOKEN value, REQUIRED
- "subFlows", a subFlows string, OPTIONAL
- "subType", a subType string, OPTIONAL
- "type", a type string with value "fmt", "ui", "quote", "link", "image", "its:generic", or "other", OPTIONAL
- other none-core properties, OPTIONAL,

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <originalData>
    <data id="d1">%d</data>
    <data id="d2">&lt;br/></data>
  </originalData>
  <segment>
    <source>Number of entries: <ph id="1" dataRef="d1" /><ph id="2"
        dataRef="d2"/>(These entries are only the ones matching the
        current filter settings)</source>
  </segment>
</unit>

Constraints

  • The following JLIFF Module properties are explicitly allowed by the wildcard other:

    - "fs_fs", a fs_fs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - "fs_subFs", a fs_subFs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - "slr_equivStorage", a slr_equivStorage object, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_sizeInfo", a slr_sizeInfo string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_sizeInfoRef", a slr_sizeInfoRef string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.

  • No other properties MUST be used.

Processing Requirements

  • Extractors MUST NOT use the ph element to represent spanning codes.

    Rationale: Using a standalone placeholder code for a spanning code does not allow for controlling the span (for instance tag order and data integrity) when Modifying inline content and is in direct contradiction to the business logic described in Representation of the codes and normative statements included in Usage of <pc> and <sc>/<ec>

Note

It is possible although not advised to use ph to mask non translatable inline content. The preferred way of protecting portions of inline content from translation is the Core Translate Annotation. See also discussion in the ITS Module section on representing translatability inline..

4.2.3.3 anonymous object "kind" : "sc"

Start of a spanning original code.

Type: object

Used in:

- an anonymous source array or an anonynmous target array

Core properties:

- "kind", a kind string with fixed value "sc", REQUIRED
- "id", a id string with an NMTOKEN value, REQUIRED
- "canCopy". a canCopy string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canDelete", acanDelete string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canOverlap", a canOverlap string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canReorder", a canReorder string with value "yes", "no", or "firstNo", OPTIONAL with default value "yes"
- "copyOf", a copyOf string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "dataRef", a dataRef string with an NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "dir", a dir string with value "ltr", "rtl", or "auto", OPTIONAL
- "disp", a disp string, OPTIONAL
- "equiv", a equiv string, OPTIONAL
- "isolated", a isolated string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "subFlows", a subFlows string, OPTIONAL
- "subType", a subType string, OPTIONAL
- "type", a type string with value "fmt", "ui", "quote", "link", "image", "its:generic", or "other", OPTIONAL
- other none-core properties, OPTIONAL,

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <segment>
    <source><sc id="1" type="fmt" subType="xlf:b"/>
        First sentence. </source>
  </segment>
  <segment>
    <source>Second sentence.<ec startRef="1" type="fmt"
        subType="xlf:b"/></source>
  </segment>
</unit>

Constraints

  • The following JLIFF Module properties are explicitly allowed by the wildcard other:

    - "fs_fs", a fs_fs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - "fs_subFs", a fs_subFs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - "slr_storageRestriction", a slr_storageRestriction object, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_sizeRestriction", a slr_sizeRestriction object, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_equivStorage", a slr_equivStorage object, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_sizeInfo", a slr_sizeInfo string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_sizeInfoRef", a slr_sizeInfoRef string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.

  • The following optional JLIFF Extension property is allowed:

    - "userdata", a userdata object.

  • No other properties MUST be used.

  • The values of the properties canCopy, canDelete, canReorder and canOverlap MUST be the same as the values the ones in the ec element corresponding to this start code.

  • The property isolated MUST be set to "yes" if and only if the ec element corresponding to this start marker is not in the same unit, and set to "no" otherwise.

Processing Requirements

  • Extractors MUST NOT use an sc / ec pair to represent standalone codes.

    Rationale: Using a spanning code for a standalone code can easily result in having text inside a span where the original format does not allow it.

4.2.3.4 ec

End of a spanning original code.

Type: object.

This element is always empty.

Parents: [Note: should be called Used in perhaps? There is no parent object, but an array]

source array, target array, <pc> and <mrk>

Properties:

- "kind", a kind string with fixed value "ec", REQUIRED
- "canCopy". a canCopy string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canDelete", acanDelete string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canOverlap", a canOverlap string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "canReorder", a canReorder string with value "yes", "no", or "firstNo", OPTIONAL with default value "yes"
- "copyOf", a copyOf string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "dataRef", a dataRef string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "dir", a dir string with value "ltr", "rtl", or "auto", OPTIONAL
- "disp", a disp string, OPTIONAL
- "equiv", a equiv string, OPTIONAL
- "id", a id string with NMTOKEN value, OPTIONAL
- "isolated", a isolated string with value "yes" or "no", OPTIONAL
- "startRef", a startRef string with NMTOKEN value, REQUIRED
- "subFlows", a subFlows string, OPTIONAL
- "subType", a subType string, OPTIONAL
- "type", a type string with value "fmt", "ui", "quote", "link", "image", "its:generic", or "other", OPTIONAL
- attributes from other namespaces, OPTIONAL

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <originalData>
    <data id="d1">\b </data>
    <data id="d2">\i </data>
    <data id="d3">\b0 </data>
    <data id="d4">\i0 </data>
  </originalData>
  <segment>
    <source>Text in <sc id="1" dataRef="d1"/>bold <sc id="2"
        dataRef="d2"/> and<ec startRef="1" dataRef="d3"/>
         italics<ec startRef="2" dataRef="d4"/>. </source>
  </segment>
</unit>

Constraints

  • The following JLIFF Module properties are explicitly allowed by the wildcard other:

    - "fs_fs", a fs_fs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - "fs_subFs", a fs_subFs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - "slr_equivStorage", a slr_equivStorage object, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_sizeInfo", a slr_sizeInfo string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
    - "slr_sizeInfoRef", a slr_sizeInfoRef string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.

    - attributes from the namespace urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:fs:2.0, OPTIONAL, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
    - attributes from the namespace urn:oasis:names:tc:xliff:sizerestriction:2.0, OPTIONAL, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.

  • No other properties MUST be used.

  • The values of the properties canCopy, canDelete and canOverlap MUST be the same as the values the ones in the sc element corresponding to this end code.

  • The value of the property canReorder MUST be "no" if the value of canReorder is "firstNo" in the sc element corresponding to this end code.

  • The property isolated MUST be set to "yes" if and only if the sc element corresponding to this end code is not in the same unit and set to "no" otherwise.

  • If and only if the property isolated is set to "yes", the property id MUST be used instead of the property startRef that MUST be used otherwise.

  • If and only if the property isolated is set to "yes", the property dir MAY be used, otherwise the property dir MUST NOT be used on the ec element.

Processing Requirements

  • Extractors MUST NOT use the sc / ec pair to represent standalone codes.

    Rationale: Using a spanning code for a standalone code can easily result in having text inside a span where the original format does not allow it.

4.2.3.5 sm

Start marker of an annotation where the spanning marker cannot be used for wellformedness reasons.

Type: object

Used in:

- an anonymous source array or an anonynmous target array

Core properties:

- "kind", a kind string with fixed value "sm", REQUIRED
- "id", a id string with NMTOKEN value, REQUIRED
- "type", a type string with value "fmt", "ui", "quote", "link", "image", "its:generic", or "other", OPTIONAL
- "translate", a translate string with value "yes" or "no", REQUIRED
- "ref", a ref string with IRI value, OPTIONAL
- "value", a value string, OPTIONAL
- other none-core properties, OPTIONAL,

Constraints

  • The following JLIFF Module properties are explicitly allowed by the wildcard other:

    • Properties allowed in both JLIFF 2.1 and JLIFF 2.0:

      - "fs_fs", a fs_fs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
      - "fs_subFs", a fs_subFs string, provided that the Constraints specified in the Format Style Module are met.
      - "slr_storageRestriction", a slr_storageRestriction object, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.
      - "slr_sizeRestriction", a slr_sizeRestriction object, provided that the Constraints specified in the Size and Length Restriction Module are met.

    • Properties allowed only in JLIFF 2.1:

      - "its_allowedCharacters", a itsm_allowedCharacters string.
      - "its_localeFilterList", a itsm_localeFilterList string with default value "*" (U+002A).
      - "its_localeFilterType", a itsm_localeFilterType string with default value "include".
      - "its_locQualityIssueComment", a itsm_locQualityIssueComment string.
      - "its_locQualityIssueEnabled", a itsm_locQualityIssueEnabled string with value "yes" or "no".
      - "its_locQualityIssueProfileRef", a itsm_locQualityIssueProfileRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_locQualityIssuesRef", a itsm_locQualityIssuesRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_locQualityIssueSeverity", a itsm_locQualityIssueSeverity number between 0 and 100, inclusive.
      - "its_locQualityIssueType", a itsm_locQualityIssueType string with value "terminology", "mistranslation", "omission", "untranslated", "addition", "duplication", "inconsistency", "grammar", "legal", "register", "locale-specific-content", "locale-violation", "style", "characters", "misspelling", "typographical", "formatting", "inconsistent-entities", "numbers", "markup", "pattern-problem", "whitespace", "internationalization", "length", "non-conformance", "uncategorized", or "other".
      - "its_locQualityRatingProfileRef", a its_locQualityRatingProfileRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_locQualityRatingScore", a its_locQualityRatingScore number between 0 and 100 inclusive.
      - "its_locQualityRatingScoreThreshold", a its_locQualityRatingScoreThreshold number between 0 and 100 inclusive.
      - "its_locQualityRatingVote", a its_locQualityRatingVote integer.
      - "its_locQualityRatingVoteThreshold", a its_locQualityRatingVoteThreshold integer.
      - "its_termConfidence", a its_termConfidence number between 0 and 1, inclusive.
      - "its_mtConfidence", a its_mtConfidencenumber between 0 and 1, inclusive.
      - "its_annotatorsRef", a its_annotatorsRef object.
      - "its_org", a its_org string.
      - "its_orgRef", a its_orgRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_person", a its_person string.
      - "its_personRef", a its_personRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_provenanceRecordsRef", a its_provenanceRecordsRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_revOrg", a its_revOrg string.
      - "its_revOrgRef", a its_revOrgRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_revPerson", a its_revPerson string.
      - "its_revPersonRef", a its_revPersonRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_revTool", a its_revTool string.
      - "its_revToolRef", a its_revToolRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_tool", a its_tool string.
      - "its_toolRef", a its_toolRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_provenanceRecords", a non-empty array of its_provenanceRecords objects.
      - "its_taClassRef", a its_taClassRef string with IRI value.
      - "its_taConfidence", a its_taConfidence number between 0 and 1 inclusive.
      - "its_taSource", a its_taSource string.
      - "its_taIdent", a its_taIdent string.
      - "its_taIdentRef", a its_taIdentRef string with IRI value.
      - "itsm_domains", a itsm_domains a non-empty array of non-empty strings not containing the , chatacter (U+002C).

    • Properties allowed only in JLIFF 2.0:

      None.

  • The following optional JLIFF Extension property is allowed:

    - "userdata", a userdata object.

  • No other properties are permitted.

See the Annotations section for more details and examples on how to use the sm object.

4.2.3.6 em

End marker of an annotation where the spanning marker cannot be used for wellformedness reasons.

Type: object.

This element is always empty.

Parents: [Note: should be called Used in perhaps? There is no parent object, but an array]

source array, target array, <pc> and <mrk>

Properties:

- "kind", a kind string with fixed value "em", REQUIRED
- "startRef", a startRef string with NMTOKEN value, REQUIRED

Constraints

  • The following JLIFF Module properties are explicitly allowed by the wildcard other:

    - "its_allowedCharacters", a its_allowedCharacters string.

See the Annotations section for more details and examples on how to use the <em> element.

4.3 Attributes

This section lists all the various attributes used in XLIFF core elements.

4.3.1 XLIFF Attributes

The attributes defined in XLIFF 2.0 are: appliesTo, canCopy, canDelete, canOverlap, canReorder, canResegment, category, copyOf, dataRef, dir, disp, equiv, hex, href, id, isolated, kind, name, order, original, priority, ref, srcDir, srcLang, startRef, state, subFlows, subFlowsEnd, subFlowsStart, subState, subType, trgLang, translate, trgDir, type, value and version.

4.3.1.1 appliesTo

Comment target - indicates the property to what the content of the note applies.

Type: string.

Value description: "source" or "target".

Default value: undefined.

Used in: note.

4.3.1.2 canCopy

Replication editing hint - indicates whether or not the inline code can be copied.

Type: string.

Value description: "yes" if the code can be copied, "no" if the code is not intended to be copied.

Default value: "yes".

Used in: sc, ec, ph.

4.3.1.3 canDelete

Deletion editing hint - indicates whether or not the inline code can be deleted.

Type: string.

Value description: "yes" if the code can be deleted, "no" if the code is not allowed to be deleted.

Default value: "yes".

Used in: sc, ec, ph.

4.3.1.4 canOverlap

Code can overlap - indicates whether or not the spanning code where this string is used can enclose partial spanning codes (i.e. a start code without its corresponding end code, or an end code without its corresponding start code).

Type: string.

Value description: "yes" or "no".

Default value: "yes".

Used in: sc and ec

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <originalData>
    <data id="1">\i1 </data>
    <data id="2">\i0 </data>
    <data id="3">{\b </data>
    <data id="4">}</data>
  </originalData>
  <segment>
    <source><pc id="1" dataRefStart="3" dataRefEnd="4" canOverlap="no">
        Bold, <sc id="2" dataRef="1" canOverlap="yes"/>both</pc>,
         italics<ec startRef="2" dataRef="2"/></source>
  </segment>
</unit>

"subfiles": [
  {
    "id": "1",
    "originalData": {
      "1": "\\i1 ",
      "2": "\\i0 ",
      "3": "{\\b ",
      "4": "}"
    },
    "subunits": [
      {
        "kind": "segment",
        "source": [
          { "id": "1", "kind": "sc", "dataRef": "3", "canOverlap": "no" },
          { "text": "Bold, " },
          { "id": "2", "kind": "sc", "dataRef": "1", "canOverlap": "yes" },
          { "text": "both" },
          { "id": "4", "kind": "ec", "startRef": "1", "dataRef": "4" },
          { "text": ", italics" },
          { "id": "5", "kind": "ec", "startRef": "2", "dataRef": "2" }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }
]
4.3.1.5 canReorder

Re-ordering editing hint - indicates whether or not the inline code can be re-ordered. See Editing Hints section for more details.

Type: string.

Value description: "yes" in case the code can be re-ordered, "firstNo" when the code is the first element of a sequence that cannot be re-ordered, "no" when it is another element of such a sequence.

Default value: "yes".

Used in: sc, ec, ph.

4.3.1.6 canResegment

Can resegment - indicates whether or not the source text in the scope of the given canResegment flag can be reorganized into a different structure of segment objects within the same parent unit.

Type: string.

Value description: "yes" or "no".

Default value: default values for this string depend on the object in which the "canResegment" property is used:

  • When used in file:

    The value "yes".

  • When the "canResegment" property is used in any other object:

    The value of the canResegment string of its parent object.

Used in: file group unit, and segment.

4.3.1.7 category

Category - provides a way to categorize notes.

Type: string.

Value description: text.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: note.

4.3.1.8 copyOf

Reference to base code - holds the id of the base code of a copied code.

Type: string.

Value description: NMTOKEN. The id value of the base code of which this code is a copy.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: ph, sc, ec.

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <segment>
    <source>Äter <pc id="1">katter möss</pc>?</source>
    <target>Do <pc id="1">cats</pc> eat <pc id="2" copyOf="1">
        mice</pc>? </target>
  </segment>
</unit>

"subfiles": [
  {
    "id": "1",
    "subunits": [
      {
        "kind": "segment",
        "source": [
          { "text": "Äter" },
          { "id": "1", "kind": "sc" },
          { "text", "katter möss" },
          { "id": "2", "kind": "ec", "startRef": "1" },
          { "text": "?" }
        ],
        "target": [
          { "text": "Do " },
          { "id": "1", "kind": "sc" },
          { "text": "cats" },
          { "kind": "ec", "startRef": "1" },
          { "text": " eat " },
          { "id": "2", "kind": "sc", "copyOf": "1" },
          { "text": "mice" },
          { "kind": "ec", "startRef": "2" },
          { "text": "?" }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }
]
4.3.1.9 dataRef property

Original data reference - holds the NMTOKEN key to the original data string contained in the unit level "originalData" vocabulary object that contains the original data for a given inline code.

Type: string.

Value description: NMTOKEN: a string matching the pattern [-._:A-Za-z0-9]+.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: ph, sc, ec.

Constraints

  • The dataRef property value MUST be one of the NMTOKEN key properties of the "originalData" object in the same anonymous unit object, to which it points to.

Processing Requirements

  • Agents processing the "dataref" property pointers MUST also lookup the NMTOKEN keys in the corresponding originalDataDir vocabulary object, if and only if such an object exists within the same same anonymous unit object.

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <originalData>
    <data id="d1">{0}</data>
    <data id="d2">{1}</data>
  </originalData>
  <segment>
    <source>Error in '<ph id="1" dataRef="d1"/>' and '<ph id="2" dataRef="d2"/>'.</source>
    <target>Erreur dans '<ph id="1" dataRef="d1"/>' et '<ph id="1" dataRef="d1"/>'.</target>
  </segment>
</unit>

"subfiles": [
  {
    "id": "1",
    "originalData": { "d1": "{0}", "d2" : "{1}" },
    "subunits": [
      {
        "kind": "segment",
        "source": [
          { "text": "Error in '" },
          { "id": "1", "kind": "ph", "dataRef": "d1"},
          { "text" : "' and '"},
          { "id": "2", "kind": "ph", "dataRef": "d2"},
          { "text": "'." }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }
]

The example above shows two ph objects that have their original data stored outside the content, in an "originaldata" vocabulary object.

4.3.1.10 dir

Directionality - indicates the directionality of content.

Type: string.

Value description: "ltr" (Left-To-Right), "rtl" (Right-To-Left), or "auto" (determined heuristically, based on the first strong directional character in scope, see [UAX #9]).

Default value: default values for this attribute depend on the element in which it is used:

  • When used in a <pc>, sc, or ec object that has a source object as its parent:

    The value of the srcDir string of the unit object, in which the "dir" properties are located.

  • When used in a <pc>, sc, or ec object that has a target object as its parent:

    The value of the trgDir string of the unit object, in which the "dir" properties are located.

  • When used in a <pc>, <sc>, or <ec> object that has a <pc> element as its parent:

    The value of the dir attribute of the parent <pc> element.

  • When used in <data>:

    The value "auto".

Used in: <data>, pc, sc, and ec.

4.3.1.11 disp

Display text - holds an alternative user-friendly display representation of the original data of the inline code.

Type: string.

Value description: text.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: ph, sc, ec.

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <originalData>
    <data id="d1">{1}</data>
  </originalData>
  <segment>
    <source>Welcome back <ph id="1" disp="[UserName]" dataRef="d1"/>!
        </source>
  </segment>
</unit>

"subfiles": [
  {
    "id": "1",
    "originalData": { "d1": "{1}" },
    "subunits": [
      {
        "kind": "segment",
        "source": [
          { "text": "Welcome back " },
          { "id": "1", "kind": "ph", "disp": "[UserName]", "dataRef": "d1" },
          { "text": "!" }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }
]

Note

To provide a plain text equivalent of the code, use the equiv property.

4.3.1.12 equiv

Equivalent text - holds a plain text representation of the original data of the inline code that can be used when generating a plain text representation of the content.

Type: string.

Value description: text.

Default value: an empty string "".

Used in: ph, sc, ec.

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <originalData>
    <data id="d1">&amp;</data>
  </originalData>
  <segment>
    <source>Open <ph id="1" equiv="" dataRef="d1"/>File</source>
  </segment>
</unit>

"subfiles": [
  {
    "id": "1",
    "originalData": { "d1": "&" },
    "subunits": [
      {
        "kind": "segment",
        "source": [
          { "text": "Open " },
          { "id": "1", "kind": "ph", "equiv": "", "dataRef": "d1" },
          { "text": "File" }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }
]

In this example the equiv property of the ph object is used to indicate that the original data of the code can be ignored in the text representation of the string. This could, for instance, help a spell-checker tool to process the content as "Open File".

Note

To provide a user-friendly representation, use the disp property.

4.3.1.13 hex TO BE DELETED, not used in JLIFF

Hexadecimal code point - holds the value of a Unicode code point that is invalid in XML.

Value description: A canonical representation of the hexBinary [XML Schema Datatypes] data type: Two hexadecimal digits to represent each octet of the Unicode code point. The allowed values are any of the values representing code points invalid in XML, between hexadecimal 0000 and 10FFFF (both included).

Default value: undefined

Used in: <cp>.

Example:

<cp hex="001A"/><cp hex="0003"/>

The example above shows a character U+001A and a character U+0003 as they have to be represented in XLIFF.

4.3.1.14 href

ref - a pointer to the location of an external skeleton file pertaining to the enclosing file object.

Type: string.

Value description: IRI.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: skeleton.

4.3.1.15 id

Identifier - a character string used to identify an element.

Type: string.

Value description: NMTOKEN: a string matching the pattern [-._:A-Za-z0-9]+. The scope of the values for this string depends on the object in which the "id" property is used.

  • When used in a file object:

    The value of the "id" property strings MUST be unique among all file id string values within the enclosing jliff object.

  • When used in group object:

    The value of the "id" property strings MUST be unique among all group id string values within the enclosing file object.

  • When used in unit object:

    The value of the "id" property strings MUST be unique among all unit id string values within the enclosing file object.

  • When used in note objects:

    The value of the "id" property strings MUST be unique among all note id string values within the immediate enclosing file, group, or unit object.

  • When used in segment, ignorable, <mrk>, sm, <pc>, sc, ec, or ph elements:

    • The inline elements enclosed by a target object MUST use the duplicate id string values of their corresponding inline elements enclosed within the sibling source object if and only if those corresponding elements exist.

    • Except for the above exception, the value MUST be unique among all of the above within the enclosing unit object.

Note

All of the above defined uniqueness scopes ignore Module and Extension data. It would be impossible to impose those uniqueness requirements onto Module or Extension data. As Core only Modifiers could inadvertently cause conflicts with Modules or Extensions based data they cannot access. Modules and Extensions reusing Core need to specify their own uniqueness scopes for the xlf:id. In general, Modules and Extensions are advised to mimic the Core uniqueness requirement within their specific wrapper elements enclosing the reused Core elements or attributes, yet Module or Extensions are free to set wider uniqueness scopes if it makes business sense for processing.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: file, group, unit, note, segment, ignorable, <data>, sc, ec, ph, <pc>, <mrk> and sm.

4.3.1.16 isolated

Orphan code flag - indicates if the start or end marker of a spanning inline code is not in the same unit as its corresponding end or start code.

Type: string.

Value description: "yes" if this start or end code is not in the same unit as its corresponding end or start code, "no" if both codes are in the same unit.

Default value: "no".

Used in: sc, ec.

Example:


<file id="f2" xmlns:abc="urn:abc">
  <unit id="1">
    <mtc:matches>
      <mtc:match id="tc01" ref="seg2">
        <source><sc id="1" isolated="yes"/>Warning:</source>
        <target><sc id="1" isolated="yes"/>Attention :</target>
      </mtc:match>
    </mtc:matches>
    <segment id="seg2">
      <source><pc id="1">Warning: File not found.</pc></source>
    </segment>
  </unit>
</file>

{
  "files": [
    {
      "id": "f2",
      "subfiles": [
        {
          "id": "1",
          "mtc_matches": {
            "matches": [
              {
                "id": "tc01",
                "ref": "seg2",
                "source": [
                  { "id": "1", "kind": "sc", "isolated": "yes" },
                  { "text": "Warning:" }
                ],
                "target": [
                  { "id": "1", "kind": "sc", "isolated": "yes" },
                  { "text": "Attention :" }
                ]
              }
            ]
          },
          "subunits": [
            {
              "id": "seg2",
              "kind": "segment",
              "source": [
                { "id": "1", "kind": "sc" },
                { "text": "Warning: File not found." },
                { "kind": "ec", "startRef": "1" }
              ]
            }
          ]
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}

In the example above the sc objects have their isolated strings of their "isolated" property set to "yes" because they do not have their corresponding ec objects.

4.3.1.17 kind TO DO

Indicates the type of an object.

Type: string.

Value description:

Default value: none.

Used in:

4.3.1.18 name

Resource name - the original identifier of the resource corresponding to the Extracted unit or group.

For example: the key in the key/value pair in a Java properties file, the ID of a string in a Windows string table, the index value of an entry in a database table, etc.

Type: string.

Value description: text.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: unit and group.

4.3.1.19 "targetOrder" property

target order - indicates the order, in which to compose the target content parts.

Type: number.

Value description: positive integer.

Default value: implicit, see below

When targetOrder is not explicitly set, the order of the target content is the natural one, i.e. it corresponds to its sibling source property conetnt, i.e. it is not being moved anywhere when composing the target content of the enclosing anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit" and the implicit targetOrder value the ordinal number (expressed as a positive integer) of that position within the anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit".

Used in: anonymous subunit object "kind" : "segment" and anonymous subunit object "kind" : "ignorable".

Constraints

  • The value of the targetOrder property MUST be unique within the enclosing anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit".

  • The value of each of the targetOrder attributes used within a anonymous subitem object "kind" : "unit" MUST NOT be higher than N, where N is the number of all current anonymous subunit objects "kind" : "segment" and anonymous subunit objects "kind" : "ignorable".

See the Segments Order section for the normative usage description.

4.3.1.20 original

Original file - a pointer to the location of the original document from which the content of the enclosing file object is extracted.

Type: string.

Value description: IRI.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: file.

4.3.1.21 priority

Priority - provides a way to prioritize notes.

Type: number.

Value description: integer between 1 and 10, inclusive.

Default value: 1.

Used in: note.

Note

Please note that 1 is the highest priority that can be interpreted as an alert, e.g. an [ITS] Localization Note of the type alert. The best practice is to use only one alert per an annotated note, and the full scale of 2-10 can be used for prioritizing notes of lesser importance than the alert.

4.3.1.22 ref

Reference - holds a reference for the associated annotation.

Type: string.

Value description: A value of the [XML Schema Datatypes] type anyURI. The semantics of the value depends on the type of annotation:

  • When used in a term annotation, the URI value is referring to a resource providing information about the term.

  • When used in a translation candidates annotation, the URI value is referring to an external resource providing information about the translation candidate.

  • When used in a comment annotation, the value is referring to a note object within the same enclosing unit object.

  • When used in a custom annotation, the value is defined by each custom annotation.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: skeleton, <mrk> or sm.

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <segment>
    <source>The <pc id="1">ref</pc> attribute of a term
        annotation holds a <mrk id="m1" type="term"
        ref="http://dbpedia.org/page/Uniform_Resource_Identifier">
        URI</mrk> pointing to more information about the given
        term.</source>
  </segment>
</unit>

{
  "subfiles": [
    {
      "id": "1",
      "subunits": [
        {
          "kind": "segment",
          "source": [
            { "text": "The " },
            { "id": "1", "kind": "sc" },
            { "text": "ref" },
            { "kind": "ec", "startRef": "1" },
            { "text": " attribute of a term annotation holds a " },
            { "id": "m1", "kind": "sm", "type": "term",
              "ref": "http://dbpedia.org/page/Uniform_Resource_Identifier" },
            { "text": "URI" },
            { "kind": "em", "startRef": "m1" },
            { "text": " pointing to more information about the given term." }
          ]
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
4.3.1.23 srcDir

Source directionality - indicates the directionality of the source content.

Type: string.

Value description: "ltr" (Left-To-Right), "rtl" (Right-To-Left), or "auto" (determined heuristically, based on the first strong directional character in scope, see [UAX #9]).

Default value: default values for this string depend on the object in which it is used:

  • When used in file:

    The value "auto".

  • When used in any other element:

    The value of the "srcDir" property srcDir string of its parent object.

Used in: file, group, and unit.

4.3.1.24 srcLang

Source language - the code of the language, in which the text to be Translated is expressed.

Type: string.

Value description: a language code as described in [BCP 47].

Default value: undefined.

Used in: jliff.

4.3.1.25 startRef

Start code or marker reference - The "id" property id string of the sc element or the sm element a given ec element or em element corresponds.

Type: string.

Value description: NMTOKEN: a string matching the pattern [-._:A-Za-z0-9]+.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: ec, em.

Example:

<unit id="1">
  <segment>
    <source><sc id="1"/>Bold, <sc id="2"/>both
        <ec startRef="1"/>, italics<ec startRef="2"/></source>
  </segment>
</unit>

{
  "subfiles": [
    {
      "id": "1",
      "subunits": [
        {
          "kind": "segment",
          "source": [
            { "id": "1", "kind": "sc" },
            { "text": "Bold, " },
            { "id": "2", "kind": "sc" },
            { "text": "both" },
            { "kind": "ec", "startRef": "1" },
            { "text": ", italics" },
            { "kind": "ec", "startRef": "2" }
          ]
        }
      ]
    }  
  ]
}
4.3.1.26 state

State - indicates the state of the translation of a segment.

Type: string.

Value description: the value MUST be set to one of the following values:

"initial" - indicates the segment is in its initial state.
"translated" - indicates the segment has been translated.
"reviewed" - indicates the segment has been reviewed.
"final" - indicates the segment is finalized and ready to be used.

The 4 defined states constitute a simple linear state machine that advances in the above given order. No particular workflow or process is prescribed, except that the three states more advanced than the default initial assume the existence of a Translation within the segment. One can further specify the state of the Translation using the subState attribute.

Default value: "initial".

Used in: segment

Processing Requirements

  • Writers MUST NOT set the state attribute values to other than the default "initial" if and only if the segment object where the property is set doesn't have the target child.

  • Writers updating the property state MUST also update or delete subState.

Note

state is an OPTIONAL property of segments with a default value and segmentation can change as the JLIFF roundtrip progresses, hence implementers don't have to make explicit use of the property. However setting of the property is advantageous if a workflow needs to make use of Advanced Validation methods.

4.3.1.27 subFlows

Sub-flows list - holds a list of id attributes corresponding to the unit objects that contain the sub-flows for a given inline code.

Type: string.

Value description: A list of NMTOKEN values separated by spaces, where NMTOKEN is a string matching the pattern [-._:A-Za-z0-9]+.Each value corresponds to the id attribute of a unit object.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: ph, sc, ec.

Example:

See the example in the Sub-Flows section.

4.3.1.28 subFlowsEnd [NOT USED]

Sub-flows list - holds a list of id attributes corresponding to the <unit> elements that contain the sub-flows for the end marker of a given inline code.

Value description: A list of NMTOKEN values separated by spaces. Each value corresponds to the id attribute of a <unit> element.

Default value: undefined

Used in: <pc>.

Example:

See the example in the Sub-Flows section.

4.3.1.29 subFlowsStart [NOT USED]

Sub-flows list - holds a list of id attributes corresponding to the <unit> elements that contain the sub-flows for the start marker of a given inline code.

Value description: A list of NMTOKEN values separated by spaces. Each value corresponds to the id attribute of a <unit> element.

Default value: undefined

Used in: <pc>.

Example:

See the example in the Sub-Flows section.

4.3.1.30 subState

subState - indicates a user-defined status for the segment object.

Type: string.

Value description:

A string value composed of a prefix and a sub-value separated by a character : (U+003A).

The prefix is a string uniquely identifying a collection of values for a specific authority. The sub-value is any string value defined by an authority.

The prefix xlf is reserved for this specification.

Other prefixes and sub-values MAY be defined by the users.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: segment

Constraints

  • If the property subState is used, the property state MUST be explicitly set.

Processing Requirements

  • Writers updating the property state MUST also update or delete subState.

4.3.1.31 subType

subType - indicates the secondary level type of an inline code.

Type: string.

Value description:

The value is composed of a prefix and a sub-value separated by a character : (U+003A).

The prefix is a string uniquely identifying a collection of sub-values for a specific authority. The sub-value is any string value defined by the authority.

The prefix xlf is reserved for this specification, and the following sub-values are defined:

xlf:lb - Line break
xlf:pb - Page break
xlf:b - Bold
xlf:i - Italics
xlf:u - Underlined
xlf:var - Variable

Other prefixes and sub-values MAY be defined by the users.

Default value: undefined.

Used in: <pc>, sc, ec and ph

Constraints

  • If the property subType is used, the property type MUST be specified as well.

  • The reserved xlf: prefixed values map onto the type property values as follows:

    For xlf:b, xlf:i, xlf:u, xlf:lb, and xlf:pb, the REQUIRED value of the type property is "fmt".
    For xlf:var, the REQUIRED value of the type property is "ui".

Processing Requirements

  • Modifiers updating the property type MUST also update or delete subType.

4.3.1.32 trgLang

Target language - the code of the language, in which the Translated text is expressed.

Type: string.

Value description: A language code as described in [BCP 47].

Default value: undefined.

Used in: jliff.

4.3.1.33 translate

Translate - indicates whether or not the source text in the scope of the given translate flag is intended for Translation.

Type: string.

Value description: "yes" or "no".

Default value: default values for this attribute depend on the element in which it is used:

  • When used in file:

    The value "yes".

  • When used in any other admissible structural element (group or unit):

    The value of the translate property of its parent object.

  • When used in annotations markers <mrk> or sm:

    The value of the translate attribute of the innermost <mrk> or unit object, in which the marker in question is located.

Used in: file group unit, <mrk> and sm.

4.3.1.34 trgDir

Target directionality - indicates the directionality of the target content.

Type: string.

Value description: "ltr" (Left-To-Right), "rtl" (Right-To-Left), or "auto" (determined heuristically, based on the first strong directional character in scope, see [UAX #9]).

Default value: default values for this attribute depend on the element in which it is used:

  • When used in file:

    The value "auto".

  • When used in any other element:

    The value of the trgDir attribute of its parent element.

Used in: file, group, and unit.

4.3.1.35 codeType [NOTE: should split into two files: codeType and mrkType]

codeType - indicates the type of an element.

Type: string.

Value description: allowed values for this attribute depend on the element in which it is used.

  • When used in <pc> , sc , ec or ph :

    The value MUST be set to one of the following values:

    "fmt" - Formatting (e.g. a <b> element in HTML)
    "ui" - User interface element
    "quote" - Inline quotation (as opposed to a block citation)
    "link" - Link (e.g. an <a> element in HTML)
    "image" - Image or graphic
    "other" - Type of element not covered by any of the other top-level types.

    Example: 

    <segment>
  <source xml:lang="cs"><pc type="quote">Blázen,
      chce dobýt točnu v takovém počasí</pc>, dodal slovy svého
      oblíbeného imaginárního autora.</source>
  <target xml:lang="en"><pc type="quote">Madman, he wants to conquer the
      pole in this weather</pc>, offered he the words of his
      favourite imaginary playwright.</target>
</segment>
"subunits": [
    {
        "kind": "segment",
        "state": "translated",
        "source": [
            { "id": "c1", "kind": "ph", "codeType": "quote", "dataRef": "d1" },
            { "text": "Blázen, chce dobýt točnu v takovém počasí," }.
            { "id": "c2", "kind": "sc", "dataRef": "d2" },       
            { "text": "dodal slovy svého oblíbeného imaginárního autora." },
            { "startRef": "c2", "kind": "ec", "dataRef": "d3" }
        ],
        "target": [
            { "id": "c1", "kind": "ph", "codeType": "quote", "dataRef": "d1" },
            { "text": "Madman, he wants to conquer the pole in this weather," },
            { "id": "c2", "kind": "sc", "dataRef": "d2" },       
            { "text": "offered he the words of his favourite imaginary playwright." },
            { "startRef": "c2", "kind": "ec", "dataRef": "d3" }
        ],
        "sourceXmlLang": "cs",
        "targetXmlLang": "en"
    }
]

    One can further specify the type of a code using the subType attribute.

    Default value: Undefined.

  • When used in <mrk> or sm :

    One of the following values: "generic", "comment", "term", or a user-defined value that is composed of a prefix and a sub-value separated by a character : (U+003A).
